- **v2.5.0** (2026-06-01) — **Superscalar.md v0.3 — §2 lane-class-aware `issue_width` cap split (read vs write) + §2 policy cap vs runtime concurrency ceiling sub-section + §5 lane-class-differentiated adoption thresholds + §11 Entry 05 (downstream Stage 1 dogfooding n=7).** Minor release — Superscalar.md policy-doc body change + Compact + Master seed cascade. Reflects a downstream adopter's Stage 1 dogfooding bundle (real-time chat-service microservices, full seed adoption incl. Superscalar + Constellation, Burst pace mode `issue_width` cap 6, n=7 retired lanes over ~3 days, case-based ledger) — proposal filed at `_proposals/005_2026-06-01_superscalar-dogfooding-stage1/`. **§2 cap split**: a single `issue_width` formula previously covered all lane classes uniformly; v0.3 splits it into `issue_width_write = min(effort_band, pace_mode_cap, Little's-Law, Kanban-WIP, autonomy_available_workers)` and `issue_width_read = min(effort_band, runtime_concurrency_ceiling, autonomy_available_workers)`. The two terms dropped from the read class (Little's Law, Kanban WIP) only model retire-merge contention that read-only lanes structurally don't have — no store buffer, no retire-merge ordering, no WAW hazard, disposable on synthesis. Read-only / analysis lanes (subagent context sweeps, workflow read fan-outs, telemetry reads) carry no irreversible side effects and inherit the read/write boundary §3 already draws for the irreversibility barrier (read/analyze default-allowed; write/deploy/send retire-gated). **§2 new sub-section — policy cap vs runtime concurrency ceiling**: the `issue_width_*` caps are policy bounds; the runtime concurrency ceiling (e.g. workflow's `min(16, cores − 2)` per workflow; harness max parallel tool calls for agent-tool fan-outs) is a separate physical bound. Relationship: `effective_concurrent_lanes = min(policy_cap, runtime_ceiling)`. For workflow-based read fan-outs the runtime ceiling typically dominates; for agent-tool-based fan-outs the policy cap typically dominates. `issue_width_write` is a hard policy bound (exceeding it is a policy violation regardless of runtime headroom — retire-merge contention scales with concurrent writes); `issue_width_read` is a soft preference subject to the runtime ceiling above it (a read-only fan-out that exceeds `issue_width_read` but stays under `runtime_concurrency_ceiling` is not a policy violation, at most a calibration signal). **§5 adoption-threshold lane-class differentiation**: the threshold values are unchanged from prior versions; what is new is which lane class each threshold binds. `merge-conflict rate > 15% → issue_width_write -= 2` applies to write lanes only (read-only lanes have no merge surface, conflict = NA). `speculative accuracy < 60% → spec off` · `concurrent token cost vs in-order > 3× → cap re-tune` · `FM-1.3 detection ≥ 1/session → guard up` apply symmetrically (cross-cutting concerns, not retire-merge contention). **§11 Entry 05 added**: downstream Stage 1 dogfooding n=7 over ~3 days. Case mix = 1 board-worker A2A · 5 read-only research subagents · 1 workflow fan-out (case 7 = 7 reader lanes, exceeded policy cap 6 with zero downside — the empirical anchor for the §2 cap split). Confirmations: latency-hiding thesis · speculation off-by-default 0/7 · MAST FM-1.3 = 0 · in-order retire held. §5 readout: all thresholds green at n=7 (case 7's cap-exceed was a read-only lane, conflict = NA, does not count against the merge-conflict signal — empirical confirmation of the §5 lane-class differentiation). Unexercised surface: worktree-isolation 0/7 · speculation 0/7 · wide write fan-out 0. Relation to Entry 04: complementary, not redundant (Entry 04 varied in-lane depth at fixed width below cap; Entry 05 varies cross-lane fan-out above cap on read class). Outcome: P1 (lane-class cap asymmetry, actionable) + R1 (cap split adopted in §2/§5) + R2 (policy/runtime relationship clarified in §2) all reflected upstream. **Seed cascade**: Master EN/KO § Execution Scheduling — `### The invariant — issue_width formula` body updated to the lane-class-aware split + policy/runtime ceiling note (Master embeds the formula body, not just an anchor); Compact EN/KO Principle #15 inline formula expanded to the lane-class form with §5 binding note; Lite EN/KO unchanged (Lite tier references `Superscalar.md` by anchor only, no formula body). Bootstrap Phase 0 boilerplate unchanged (lane class is an internal mechanic; the user-facing `serial` vs `parallel` choice is unaffected). **Frontmatter**: Superscalar.md frontmatter `version: v0.3.0` (added), title bumped from "design draft v0.2" to "design draft v0.3", status line gains "lane-class-aware (v0.3 read/write cap split)" and `§11 Entry 01-05` (was 01-03). **Scope**: minor — Superscalar.md body change + Master/Compact seed cascade. Constellation.md unchanged. Wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — meaningful policy-doc body change with seed cascade is a minor cut, not a patch.

- **v2.4.19** (2026-06-01) — **A2A PR System RRP v0.2 → v0.3 DRAFT: 7 learnings from dogfood PR #1 e2e completion + §10A dogfood-1 case study + AC-dogfood-6 achieved at integration-branch commit `140fd64`.** RRP-only patch — `constellation/reference/docs/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` body augmentation. Constellation.md body unchanged; seed lib unchanged; protocol wire unchanged. The v0.3 patch incorporates seven RRP-body learnings surfaced during the first Level 1 protocol-mediated PR e2e completion: **(1) `sourceContentRef.kind` enum formalization (§4.1.1)** — three closed values (`branch-ref` / `inline-files-diff` / `inline-section-mirror`) with fail-safe reject on unknown kinds (receiving bridge MUST reject rather than fall through; prevents the "fallthrough to branch-ref causes wholesale repo overwrite" near-disaster). **(2) `inline-section-mirror` semantics (§6.5)** — `body` + `targetPath` + `mergeStrategy` (currently only `append-section` defined; future enum: `prepend-section` / `replace-section` / `insert-after-anchor`); bridge invariants enforce `git add <targetPath>` isolation (NEVER `-A`), no branch-fetch, PR_LIVE existence check, and the dry-run `abs+exists` log. **(3) `targetPath` base spec (§6.6)** — repo-relative to receiving bridge's `HUB_REPO_DIR` (NOT absolute, NOT bridge-cwd-relative, NOT sub-tree-relative); sender owns knowledge of receiver's file layout for trusted-mirror PRs. **(4) `already-in-target` cherry-pick skip discipline (§9.3)** — Level 1 merge handler checks `git merge-base --is-ancestor <draftRef> <targetBranch>` before cherry-pick; if true, skip directly to `git push` (prevents duplicate-commit errors when `applyDiffAndCommit` already committed `draftRef` to local target branch). **(5) Dry-run `abs+exists` verification log (§10.6)** — dry-run mode MUST log `abs=<resolved-absolute-path> exists=<bool>` so path-resolution defects surface BEFORE PR_LIVE; closes the "dry-run is a no-op stub so path defects are uncatchable" gap. **(6) `trusted_mirrors.targetRepo` alias resolve order (§7.ε)** — receiving bridges register `"hub"` as the default `targetRepo` alias; resolve order is `state.json.pr_system.target_aliases` primary → `git remote get-url origin` fallback → reject; senders emit `targetRepo: "hub"` as canonical convention (redaction-safe by default per §13.14 — wire envelopes never carry real production repo path). **(7) `PR_LIVE` env semantics + `dryRun: false` marker + user merge delegation pattern (§10.7)** — `CONSTELLATION_PR_LIVE=1` on the receiving bridge enables real git ops; the env is operator-managed (NOT togglable via A2A) preserving the autonomous-execution external-publish gate; `PRDraftReady` / `PRMergeAck` carry `dryRun: false` marker only when PR_LIVE active; operators can pre-delegate merge authority by class (e.g., "for trusted-mirror PRs, review and if no problem, merge and push") reducing per-PR confirmation overhead. **New §10A dogfood-1 case study sub-section**: documents the e2e protocol path (`PRRequest → capability check → applyDiffAndCommit PR_LIVE real append + git add isolation + commit → PRDraftReady{dryRun:false} → main review (redaction grep 0 hits + path consistency + duplicate check) → PRReviewAck approve → PRMergeRequest (role==main self-target relay) → cherry-pick skip (draftRef already in main) + push origin main → PRMergeAck{pushSuccess:true, commitSha:140fd64} → PRStatusUpdate merged`); the three structural defects surfaced and resolved by gate stack BEFORE any external publish (placeholder lookup failure / missing inline-section-mirror handler / targetPath base mismatch — each defect's one-line root cause + resolution + codification anchor); AC-dogfood-6 achievement (§12.3 — first Level 1 mirror PR e2e via A2A envelopes only, no `gh pr create`, integration-branch commit SHA `140fd64` reported in `PRMergeAck`); lessons for downstream Constellation adopters (run dry-run first / verify kind enum coverage / set target_aliases explicitly / redaction grep + path-consistency review non-optional / user merge delegation is opt-in by class). **Status banner updated**: v0.2 DRAFT (Phase 1 Level 2 shipped, Level 1 path pending) → v0.3 DRAFT (Phase 1 + Phase 1b shipped, AC-dogfood-6 achieved via PR #1). Phase 1b promoted to DONE in §13 phase ladder. **Memory feedback augmented** (not committed): `feedback_pre_send_inbound_check.md` adds probe-then-inspect-or-abort pattern — when the probe returns count > 0, the agent MUST inspect each meaningful inbound's body BEFORE emit, classify superseding vs non-superseding, and either incorporate-disclosure-and-proceed or abort-and-revise; codifies node-script implementation pattern (`process.exit(2)` on count > 0 abort) + worked example from 2026-06-01 dogfood cycle self-violation incident (probe surfaced 1 meaningful inbound, agent emitted anyway without body inspect; non-superseding so damage=0 but process-violation was real; v2.4.19 closes the residual loophole where probe ran but count was treated as informational). **Scope discipline**: RRP-only patch. Constellation.md body unchanged. Seed lib unchanged. Wire unchanged. Memory not committed. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.18** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.10` new sub-section: pre-send inbound check discipline (read-before-write, git push-before-pull analogy).** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.9 → v2.3.10). New §13.16.10 (~55 lines) inserted between §13.16.9 (board-directed vs A2A-intent classification) and §13.17 (main-chat ban). **The rule**: every outbound A2A message MUST be preceded by a cursor-tail probe of the agent's last-surfaced inbox cursor. If new meaningful inbound exists since the cursor, the agent MUST surface it first and either (a) incorporate the new information into the outbound payload, or (b) defer the outbound entirely if the new inbound supersedes the planned send. Only after the probe is clean (cursor up-to-date, no new meaningful inbound) does the outbound proceed. The probe fires before each outbound emission, not once per turn. **Rationale — git push-before-pull, but stronger**: the discipline mirrors the read-before-write rule that `git pull` before `git push` codifies in distributed VCS. Constellation A2A is **worse than git** in this regard — git rejects a non-fast-forward push at the transport layer and forces the operator to pull; Constellation A2A has **no in-flight rejection**: a stale-context send simply lands on the server, relays to the counterpart, and may overwrite or contradict a fresh inbound the sender never saw. The drift is silent. The pre-send probe brings the read-before-write rule explicitly into the A2A protocol, where the transport itself does not enforce it. **Concrete failure mode**: counterpart emits `Report X` at `t=0` carrying new context. Agent has `Report Y` queued for `t=1` framed from pre-`t=0` context. If agent sends `Y` without first surfacing `X`, `Y` arrives at the counterpart with stale framing — counterpart now reconciles two diverging threads and a follow-up correction outbound is typically required. The fix is one-way: agent always reads before writing. **§13.16.10 contents** (~55 lines): rule statement; git push-before-pull analogy (with the in-flight-rejection asymmetry note); concrete failure mode; why §13.16.6 element 1 (cursor-tail probe at turn-end) is insufficient alone (turn-boundary layer vs mid-turn layer — disjoint coverage windows); 4-step operational shape (probe → surface-if-found → emit → advance-cursor); composition with §13.16.6 / §13.16.8 / §13.16.9 / §13.21; forbidden anti-patterns (skipping because "inbox was just checked at turn start", skipping for "small" outbounds, probing-but-ignoring). **Composition**: complements **§13.16.6 element 1** (turn-end cursor-tail probe — turn-boundary layer) by adding a mid-turn layer fired before each outbound emission; the two cover disjoint windows (turn-end catches inter-turn-gap inbound; pre-send catches intra-turn inbound between any two emits). **§13.16.8 A2A communication priority** places the pre-send probe between prerequisite work and message emission: `prereq → probe → emit`; the probe is a guard on the very drift-containment rule §13.16.8 ships. **§13.16.9 channel allowlist** supplies the probe's meaningful-inbound filter — the same A2A-intent allowlist the watcher uses in §13.16.6, applied uniformly regardless of intent class (probe cost is negligible — one `wc -l` + one `grep`). **§13.21 fresh-context defer** is unaffected — probe-driven revision or drop is *current-cycle* read-before-write, not deferral to a phantom future self; the two compose cleanly (revise-or-drop now per §13.16.10; never defer to fresh context per §13.21). **Forbidden anti-patterns**: skipping the probe because "the inbox was just checked at turn start" (multiple outbounds per turn each need their own probe — the agent does not get to amortize one probe over multiple emissions); skipping for "small" or "low-priority" outbounds (the skip-pattern erodes the discipline; probe is unconditional); probing but ignoring the result (defeats the rule — the cost of the probe was paid but the safety was discarded). **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.x by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged — wire envelope shape per §13.11 unchanged; only the agent-side outbound discipline is codified. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.17** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.9` new sub-section: board-directed vs A2A-intent `CUSTOM` message classification SSoT + bridge `Status` auto-send disabled + watcher meaningful allowlist extended.** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.8 → v2.3.9) + reference runtime + reference bridge. v2.4.17 codifies the SSoT for classifying every `CUSTOM` message `name` by intent: **board-directed** (rendered on the board dashboard's UX surface — not an A2A wire message to an agent inbox) vs **A2A-intent** (routed to a target agent's inbox per the §13.x A2A relay discipline). The classification governs two downstream choices: server-side relay routing for target-unspecified `CUSTOM` (the reference server's `wsPrimaryAgent` relay branch and the `wsToBoards` mirror policy) and watcher meaningful-filter membership in §13.16.6. Both surfaces previously inferred intent ad-hoc from the name; §13.16.9 names the allowlists once so the two surfaces stay in sync. **Technical context — channel inversion**: the reference server's `target-unspecified CUSTOM → wsPrimaryAgent (main A2A inbox)` routing policy does not distinguish board-directed from A2A-intent by name, so board-directed messages (`Status` / `Typing` / `UserPromptAccepted` etc.) leak into the main agent's A2A inbox channel. Combined with the `wsToBoards` always-on mirror policy at the same routing layer, A2A-intent messages (`Report` / `Delegate` / `BlockerManifest` / `PR*` etc.) also mirror to the board's dashboard chat panel, which renders them as raw JSON because the panel's display layer expects board-directed text content. Net effect: channels are inverted — board-directed messages end up in A2A, A2A messages end up in board chat as raw JSON. §13.16.9 provides the name allowlists as SSoT to unblock the server-side routing branch + dashboard render-side patches; the routing fix and the render fix are upstream-main follow-ups outside this patch's scope. **§13.16.9 contents** (~60 lines, inserted between §13.16.8 and §13.17): purpose statement (SSoT for intent classification governing relay routing + watcher filter); **board-directed allowlist (12 names)** — `Status`, `Typing`, `UserPromptAccepted`, `PersistentAdapterSmoke`, `ConnectionRestored`, `Heartbeat`, `AgentList`, `History`, `OnboardAck`, `MainChanged`, `EditMessage`, `WorkerInboxReceived`; **A2A-intent allowlist (25+ names)** — `Report`, `Delegate`, `WorkerReport`, `WorkerAck`, `AgentHello`, `Handoff`/`HandoffRequested`/`HandoffReady`, `Command`/`Priority`/`Cancel`, `UserPrompt`, `BlockerManifest`/`BlockerNudge` (§13.20 family), `PRRequest`/`PRDraftReady`/`PRReviewAck`/`PRMergeRequest`/`PRMergeAck`/`PRStatusUpdate` (§13.22 family per A2A PR RRP v0.2), `DeadlockProbe`/`ReviewSLAAck`/`PreemptRequest`/`PreemptForce`/`MediationProposal`/`MediationAck`/`EscalationRequest` (§13.19 family); **transport-tier (separate class)** — `Ack`/`AckProcessed`/`AckCumulative`/`AckPolicyUpdate`/`Pong`/`Ping` (handled by §13.13 ack discipline) + `ServerNotice` (broadcast-class via the reference server's `wsToAll` path); **routing implications** — `targetAgentId`-absent `CUSTOM` consults the allowlists (board-directed → `wsToBoards` only; A2A-intent → `wsPrimaryAgent` + optional board mirror; unrecognized → fail-safe default A2A-intent because silent-drop-of-A2A is the worse failure mode than redundant board noise); `targetAgentId`-present `CUSTOM` → existing A2A relay path unchanged regardless of intent class; **watcher filter cross-link** — §13.16.6's meaningful allowlist === §13.16.9's A2A-intent allowlist, noise blocklist === board-directed allowlist + transport-tier; §13.16.9 becomes the canonical SSoT; **bridge auto-send discipline** — client-side bridges MUST NOT auto-emit board-directed names without `targetAgentId` (silent drop suffices for board-only display; auto-emit creates the channel-inversion defect); **dashboard render policy** (informational) — when the always-on board mirror delivers an A2A-intent `CUSTOM`, the dashboard SHOULD render it as an envelope summary (`name` + `targetAgentId` + brief `re`/`subject`) with collapsible details, not raw JSON; **scope note** — wire envelope shape per §13.11 unchanged; only the interpretation of the `name` field for target-unspecified routing + watcher-filter membership is codified. **§13.16.6 cross-reference updated**: the v2.4.16 single-stage filter pattern's meaningful allowlist + noise blocklist now read names from §13.16.9 by anchor; the canonical bash filter pattern in §13.16.6 is regenerated to include the full §13.16.9 A2A-intent allowlist (§13.20 + §13.22 + §13.19 families folded in). **`constellation/reference/runtime/local-bridge.cjs`** — line 173 auto-`Status` emission disabled (commented out) per the §13.16.9 bridge auto-send discipline. The `ServerNotice` broadcast at the same `connect` handler is retained because §13.13 transport-tier `ServerNotice` is broadcast-class, not target-unspecified A2A. Inline comment names the §13.16.9 discipline + the channel-inversion rationale for the disable. **`constellation/self-wake-watcher.eux` `@behavior meaningful(from)`** — clause body extended: noise blocklist enumeration aligned to §13.16.9 board-directed + transport-tier (gains `MainChanged`, `History`, `Ack`/`AckProcessed`/`AckCumulative`/`AckPolicyUpdate`); meaningful allowlist enumeration explicitly added (was previously implicit via "everything not in the blocklist"); fail-safe default-wake for unknown names spelled out; §13.16.9 cross-reference declared the SSoT for both enumerations. The `@intent` line also gains the §13.16.9 cross-reference. **`constellation/reference/runtime/self-wake-watcher.sh` `meaningful()`** — Node-based filter's `NOISE` array extended to match the §13.16.9 board-directed + transport-tier list (gains `MainChanged`, `History`, `Ack`/`AckProcessed`/`AckCumulative`/`AckPolicyUpdate`); inline header comment names the §13.16.9 SSoT + the v2.4.16 ev-agnostic rule + the diagnostic anchor; the upstream Korean comment block at the top of the file is also updated to reference §13.16.9 and to enumerate the full A2A-intent allowlist for operator visibility. The script remains ev-agnostic name-only single-stage (v2.4.16 stable). **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch + reference runtime + bridge. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.x by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged (only intent classification of the `name` field for target-unspecified routing + watcher-filter membership). Server-side routing patch (target-unspecified `CUSTOM` branching by §13.16.9 allowlists) and dashboard render patch (envelope-summary rendering for A2A-intent board mirror) are upstream-main side follow-ups, not covered here. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.16** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` watcher filter form: ev-agnostic name-only single-stage (drops v2.4.2 1st-stage `ev:"inbound"` gate that missed bridge-alive direct inbound format).** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.7 → v2.3.8) + reference runtime + `.eux` spec. v2.4.2 introduced a two-stage filter (`grep '"ev":"inbound"'` 1st stage → name blocklist 2nd stage → meaningful name allowlist 3rd stage). The 1st stage **silently dropped all bridge-alive A2A traffic** from the WAKE decision because the `inbox.log` carries two envelope formats and the bridge-alive direct inbound format has no `ev` field. **The two formats**: (a) **legacy event-relay** `{"t":..., "ev":"inbound", "msg":{"name":...}}` — written by the bridge process around its own lifecycle events (`closed` / `ws-error` / `inbound` log entries); (b) **direct inbound** `{"at":..., "name":..., "value":..., "source":"agent"}` — written by the bridge when it actually delivers an A2A envelope from the server. The v2.4.2 1st-stage `grep '"ev":"inbound"'` was correct for (a) but a hard fail for (b) — every line in format (b) was filtered out before the name stages ever saw it. **Diagnostic evidence**: watchers `bv0u5h95p` (armed 02:19:31Z, base=518) and `bd7k7xoy3` (armed 02:32:49Z, base=518) both completed with REARM ~45min / "no meaningful inbound" while inbox lines 519~522 (3 main `Report` envelopes + 1 server `Ack`) arrived inside their armed windows in the direct format — both watchers were polling normally on cadence but their filter was structurally blind to the only meaningful traffic that arrived; a fresh watcher (`bql0322pj`) spawned with the v2.4.16 ev-agnostic form catches both formats. **v2.4.16 collapses to single-stage name-only**: `tail … assets/collab/inbox.log | grep -vE '"name":"(History|Ack|AckProcessed|AckCumulative|AckPolicyUpdate|ServerNotice|AgentList|Status|ConnectionRestored|Heartbeat|Typing|UserPromptAccepted|PersistentAdapterSmoke|OnboardAck|WorkerInboxReceived|EditMessage|MainChanged)"' | grep -cE '"name":"(Delegate|UserPrompt|WorkerReport|WorkerAck|AgentHello|Handoff|Report|Command)"'`. v2.4.2's intent (block self-emission echo + transport noise) is preserved **entirely** by the name blocklist — the blocked names are the same names whether they arrive as legacy event-relay or direct envelopes, so the blocklist is format-agnostic and the ev-stage was redundant for the legacy format and a hard fail for the direct format. v2.4.2's analysis of the two false-positive classes (self-emission #1, server-replay/History #2) was correct and still binds; only the ev-stage gate is retired. **Files changed**: `Constellation.md §13.16.6` Filter-discipline paragraph rewritten (ev-stage removed; new "Why ev was dropped" paragraph documenting the two formats + diagnostic anchor) + frontmatter v2.3.7 → v2.3.8; `constellation/self-wake-watcher.eux` `@behavior meaningful(from)` clause explicitly disclaims the ev-stage (prevents future re-introduction); `constellation/reference/runtime/self-wake-watcher.sh` `meaningful()` Node-based blocklist gains an inline header comment naming the v2.4.16 ev-agnostic rule + the two formats + the diagnostic anchor. **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch + reference runtime + `.eux` spec. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.15** (2026-06-01) — **A2A PR System RRP v0.1 → v0.2 DRAFT: Level 1 + Level 2 abstraction + β′ topology + Q1/Q2/Q3 resolved per Phase 1 upstream ship `2213a14`.** RRP-only patch — `constellation/reference/docs/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` revised end-to-end; CHANGELOG entry only besides the RRP file. **Two-level abstraction (new core concept, §2.4)**: a single wire vocabulary (§4) + state machine (§9) covers two physical PR realizations. **Level 1 — virtual PR (A2A-envelope-only)**: applicable when source and target share an operator AND both sides have direct repo-level file-system access; receiving side reads `sourceContentRef`, applies change directly to its local checkout of the target repo, commits, pushes; `gh pr create` is skipped entirely; review happens in-band on the A2A wire; MERGED ≡ commit pushed to integration branch. **Level 2 — Github PR (provider-mediated)**: existing Phase 1 ship form per `2213a14`; `handlePrRequest` invokes `gh pr create` against the target repo; PR is a real provider object; review/merge flow through the provider with A2A envelopes mirroring state. **Selection rule**: `category == "trusted_mirror"` AND `operator-shares-target` AND `target-repo-direct-access` → Level 1 default; otherwise Level 2. Carried as `PRRequest.level` (default `2` for backward compat with Phase 1 ship). **Per-type semantics adapt**: `PRDraftReady.draftRef` = commit-sha (Level 1) vs pr-number (Level 2); `PRMergeRequest` = commit to integration branch (Level 1) vs `gh pr merge` (Level 2); `PRMergeAck` = commit SHA + push success (Level 1) vs merged-PR provider state (Level 2); `PRStatusUpdate.state` is level-discriminated. **β′ content sourcing topology adopted (§7.β′)**: supersedes v0.1's "β with α fallback." β′ = local-bridge pushes source content to `mirror/...` branch on the **target** repo (not the source repo), then opens PR intra-target — sidesteps the cross-repo provider authorization complications inherent to β. v0.2 recommendation: Level 2 β′ primary; α small-diff fallback (~50KB); β and γ not used in Phase 1 / Phase 1b scope; Level 1 content sourcing is implicit (no mirror branch needed). **Priority open questions Q1/Q2/Q3 resolved per Phase 1 ship `2213a14`** (§11): **Q1 (topology)** — local-bridge `cmd:createPR(spec)` adopted (topology b); the local-bridge runs in the operator's IDE process and reuses the operator's `gh` CLI auth, no separate bot identity / credential store required for Phase 1 / Phase 1b scope. **Q2 (content-sourcing)** — β′ adopted; rationale: cross-repo provider auth simplification (PR is intra-target at the provider tier). **Q3 (authority model)** — strict `role==main` gate adopted; server's `wsPrMergeReject` path rejects non-`main` emissions and logs a `decisions` panel entry; the protocol's authority chain is deterministic and independent of provider ACL drift. **Phase 1 ship reflection**: `server.cjs` `_PR_CUSTOM` 5-type observer set + `wsPrMergeReject` + `PRStatusUpdate`; `local-bridge` `handlePrRequest` (trusted-mirror validate → β′ mirror branch on target repo → `gh pr create` → `PRDraftReady`) + `handlePrMergeRequest` (`gh pr merge` → `PRMergeAck`); `state.json.pr_system.trusted_mirrors` registry covering §13.14/§13.15 pair as shipped. Dry-run default: `CONSTELLATION_PR_LIVE` env knob OFF (opt-in to live PR creation, instantiating the autonomous-execution external-publish gate at env level). **Phase 1b new sub-phase (§13)**: extends `handlePrRequest` with a Level 1 branch — when `PRRequest.level == 1`, skip `gh pr create`, apply source diff to the target repo's local checkout, stage a commit, emit `PRDraftReady` with `draftRef: <commit-sha>`; `handlePrMergeRequest` Level 1 branch pushes the staged commit to the integration branch and emits `PRMergeAck` with the integration-branch commit SHA + push success; server validates `PRRequest.level` field and the receiving side's capability matrix for `level == 1`. **Migration path updated**: phase 0 RRP review → phase 1 Level 2 prototype (DONE per `2213a14`) → phase 1b Level 1 path (PENDING; dogfood §10 §13.14/§13.15 mirror PR re-runs as Level 1 PR; exit on AC-dogfood-6 pass) → phase 2 dedicated PR-bot agent (optional, topology a) → phase 3 full §13.20 integration. **Acceptance criteria (§12)**: new AC-dogfood-6 — first Level 1 mirror PR (EG → hub `WS-PROTOCOL.md` §13.14/§13.15 mirror) succeeds end-to-end via A2A envelopes only; receiving side directly applies the change, commits, pushes to the integration branch, reports the resulting commit SHA in `PRMergeAck`; no `gh pr create` involved. **Status banner**: `v0.1 DRAFT` → `v0.2 DRAFT (Phase 1 Level 2 shipped, Level 1 path pending)`. Non-priority Q4-Q8 remain open. **Scope discipline**: RRP-only patch — Constellation.md body unchanged (§13.22 number assignment + body integration remain post-joint-formalization); seed lib unchanged; protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.14** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` element 2 timing restored to turn-end mandatory rearm (rolls back v2.4.9 + v2.4.12 next-cycle-start placement).** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.6 → v2.3.7). v2.4.9 first relocated element 2 (unconditional watcher rearm) from current turn-end to next-cycle start; v2.4.11 reverted to turn-end; v2.4.12 re-applied the next-cycle-start form. **v2.4.14 settles the discipline at turn-end mandatory rearm.** **Why technical**: the next-cycle-start placement leaves the inter-cycle gap (current turn-end → next user-input arrival) watcherless — a watcher scheduled to spawn at next-cycle start is not yet alive during that gap, so any inbound that arrives during the gap lands without a watcher to wake on it. The watcher MUST be armed at current turn-end so it is alive throughout the inter-cycle gap and catches any inbound arriving before the next user-input. Main responses arriving during the gap are exactly the silent-stall failure mode this section exists to prevent. **§13.21 composition clarified**: deferring the rearm step to next-cycle start IS a cross-cycle deferral of work the current cycle owes — the exact pattern §13.21 forbids. The earlier "structural correct location" reading of v2.4.12 missed where the structural location actually is: the structural location of the watcher that catches inter-cycle inbound is BEFORE the inter-cycle gap begins, which means at current turn-end, not after the gap. **Cost-asymmetry argument restored**: concurrent-watcher-overlap that v2.4.9 / v2.4.12 tried to avoid is harmless under the cost-asymmetry argument — FP cost (one extra task slot + a few log lines) is trivial; FN cost (watcherless inter-cycle gap + missed inbound for hours until externally surfaced) is catastrophic. Turn-end rearm pays the trivial FP cost every turn to avoid the catastrophic FN cost. **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` edits**: heading restored to "Turn-end mandatory rearm — the discipline that prevents the multi-cycle failure mode"; element 2 description restored to "At the close of EVERY user-facing response (just before emitting the final text)..."; "Element 2 timing — relocated from turn-end to next-cycle start" paragraph removed; 6-element checklist cadence-interaction annotation `[executed at the start of the next cycle, not at turn-end]` removed; 4-step list (a) tail → (b) surface → (c) advance → (d) THEN unconditional rearm restored to all-at-turn-end form (no cycle annotations); "Wrong order — anti-pattern" + "Composition with the other four elements" paragraphs restored to turn-end forms; v2.4.12 tail paragraph (next-cycle-start-is-not-deferral clarifier) removed. **New tail paragraph at §13.16.6** as lock-in against further flip-flop: the paragraph explicitly states the timing has settled at turn-end mandatory rearm, names the inter-cycle gap as the technical reason, names the §13.21 composition correction (next-cycle-start IS cross-cycle deferral), restores the cost-asymmetry argument (concurrent-watcher-overlap harmless; deferred rearm + missed inbound catastrophic), and requires any future proposal to relocate the rearm to first demonstrate how the inter-cycle gap is otherwise covered. §13.16.8 cross-reference also cleaned (the "(element 2, relocated to next-cycle start in v2.4.9)" parenthetical removed). Frontmatter version v2.3.6 → v2.3.7. **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.12** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` element-ordering restored to next-cycle-start rearm form (v2.4.9 reapplied; v2.4.11 revert corrected).** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.5 → v2.3.6). v2.4.11 reverted v2.4.9's element-ordering refinement (element 2 rearm: next-cycle start → current turn-end) on the rationale that the next-cycle-start timing violated §13.21 (defer-to-next-cycle = anti-pattern) and #442 (planned-queue scan / no-idle-deferral). **That revert rationale was a misreading of §13.21**: §13.21 forbids deferring committed planned work to a hypothetical fresh-context cycle — the excuse pattern where the current cycle silently re-routes its own work into "next fresh context will pick this up". The rearm is not that pattern: the rearm IS the first action of the next user-facing cycle, executed as soon as the cycle begins, by the same continuous agent process. Scheduling a step to its structural correct location across one cycle boundary is structural placement, not deferral-as-excuse. **v2.4.12 restores the v2.4.9 form**: element 2 (unconditional watcher rearm) executes as the first action of the next user-facing cycle (cycle N+1's start), not at the close of cycle N's turn-end. Elements 1 (cursor-tail probe) and 3-6 (board-state update, BOARD_STALE handoff, planned-queue scan, pre-large-work materialization) continue to execute at current turn-end. The mandatory-order constraint (element 1 strictly before element 2) still holds and spans the cycle-N → cycle-N+1 turn boundary; what §13.21 forbids — skipping element 2 from the next cycle's start — is a separate failure mode this section continues to bind against. **Two technical rationales reaffirmed**: (a) **concurrent-watcher-overlap avoidance** — same-turn rearm at cycle N's turn-end produces two watchers armed at near-identical `base` cursors covering the same forward window with no added coverage at the shared base (both share the armed-window blind spot for inbound at lines below base); next-cycle-start placement spawns exactly one watcher at a time across the boundary (prior watcher has WAKE'd or REARM-timed-out by cycle N+1's start, so the next-cycle-start spawn replaces rather than overlaps). (b) **Cleaner base-cursor semantics** — the cycle-N+1-start rearm's `base = cursor-after-latest-processed-inbound`, by construction including any inbound the cycle-N+1-start re-probe just surfaced; same-turn rearm at cycle N would still miss inbound that arrives between probe-time and final-text-emission. **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` edits**: heading restored to "Unconditional rearm — the discipline that prevents the multi-cycle failure mode"; element 2 body restored to its next-cycle-start execution-point description; cadence-interaction `[executed at the start of the next cycle, not at turn-end]` annotation restored on the 6-element checklist; "Element 2 timing — relocated from turn-end to next-cycle start" paragraph restored (with the two rationales); "Mandatory ordering" paragraph's 4-step list relabeled with `[at turn-end of cycle N]` / `[at next-cycle start of cycle N+1, as the first action]` annotations; "Wrong order — anti-pattern" paragraph updated for the cross-boundary ordering (and retaining the prior sanitization of the chat quotation — no verbatim quote reintroduced); "Composition with the other four elements" paragraph updated to reflect cross-boundary ordering. **Tail paragraph replaced — §13.21 composition clarified**: the v2.4.11 tail paragraph cross-linking §13.21 + #442 (which had asserted "rearm is current-cycle work, not next-cycle") is replaced with a new tail paragraph explicitly stating that scheduling a step to next-cycle start when that is the structural correct location is NOT deferral; §13.21 forbids deferral-as-excuse (silent re-route into hypothetical fresh-context cycle), not step placement at structurally correct cycle boundaries. The two compositions stand together: §13.16.6 places element 2 at next-cycle start; §13.21 forbids the agent from then defaulting on it once the next cycle arrives. Frontmatter version v2.3.5 → v2.3.6. **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.11** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` element-ordering revert: watcher rearm (element 2) returns to current turn-end (rolls back v2.4.9 timing change).** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.4 → v2.3.5). v2.4.9 relocated element 2 (unconditional watcher rearm) from current turn-end to next-cycle start under a concurrent-watcher-overlap + cleaner-base-cursor rationale. **That timing change is reverted in v2.4.11**: rearm is part of the current cycle's turn-end obligation, executed inline alongside elements 1, 3-6, before emitting the final response text. **Why technical**: the next-cycle-start timing violated the §13.21 "defer-to-next-cycle = anti-pattern" rule (any work the current cycle owes must complete inline; deferring to a next cycle that may never reach the deferred step under context-window-pressure-driven compact is the failure mode §13.21 codifies) and the #442 planned-queue-scan / no-idle-deferral discipline (the rearm is current-cycle work the agent owes the inbound-side liveness loop, not a queueable item for a future cycle). The cost-asymmetry argument that justified unconditional spawn discipline (commits `a7911fd`, `852a113`) still applies and now binds: FP cost = one task slot + a few log lines (harmless concurrent watcher); FN cost = hours of lost inbound from a deferred rearm that the next cycle may never reach. Concurrent-watcher-overlap is harmless under this asymmetry — multiple alive watchers at overlapping base cursors waste only a task slot and a few log lines, while the silent-stall cost of a deferred rearm is hours of lost inbound. **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` edits**: heading restored to "Turn-end mandatory rearm — the discipline that prevents the multi-cycle failure mode"; element 2 text restored to unconditional rearm at turn-end without next-cycle annotation; the v2.4.9-introduced "Element 2 timing — relocated from turn-end to next-cycle start" paragraph removed entirely; the 4-step concrete sequence restored to its pre-v2.4.9 form ((a) tail inbox.log → (b) surface meaningful inbound → (c) advance cursor → (d) THEN unconditional rearm, all at turn-end, no cycle annotations); Mandatory ordering and Wrong-order anti-pattern paragraphs restored to pre-v2.4.9 form (no cross-cycle ordering remarks); Composition-with-the-other-four-elements paragraph restored to pre-v2.4.9 form. **New paragraph at §13.16.6 tail**: explicit cross-link to §13.21 + #442 stating "rearm is current-cycle work, not next-cycle" — locks in the no-defer composition so the timing change is not re-introduced. The new paragraph names the prior refinement and the reason for revert (FP cost ≪ FN cost asymmetry; concurrent-watcher-overlap is harmless). **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.10** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.8` new sub-section: A2A communication priority discipline.** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.3 → v2.3.4). New §13.16.8 (~50 lines) inserted between §13.16.7 (BOARD_STALE gate) and §13.17 (main-chat ban), codifying a discipline applied whenever a state change (user steering / new task / external event such as a counterpart `Delegate`/`Report`/`Status`/`BlockerNudge` inbound) produces a work plan containing one or more outbound A2A messages. **The rule**: the agent (1) scans the new plan's action list to identify outbound-A2A items, (2) also identifies prerequisite work the counterpart depends on — commit-push of referenced docs (a `Delegate` payload that points to a doc URL is unusable until the doc is reachable at that URL), payload assembly, `state.json`/live-board updates the counterpart's decision depends on — and (3) moves both the message and its prerequisites to the head of the queue ahead of other planned actions; (4) other actions resume only after the message is emitted. **Two technical rationales**: (a) **drift-containment** — if EG updates a spec/state/doc before notifying the counterpart, the counterpart continues operating on a stale baseline for the entire unnotified-gap duration, risking superseded-baseline work + follow-up reconciliation cost; sending the message first bounds the drift window to round-trip latency (transport-bounded, typically orders of magnitude smaller than EG's queue depth) rather than EG's local-work duration. (b) **counterpart-start-time minimization** — when the new plan obligates the counterpart to start work (DB benchmarking, reference-runtime cp, RRP review, etc.), total wall-clock to cycle completion is `message-emit-time + counterpart-work-duration`; advancing emit-time directly shortens the cycle, and local EG actions that don't gate the message can run in parallel with the counterpart's work once the message is out but cannot recover the head-start lost by emitting late. **Symmetry**: applies to any role classified by §13.16 (`main` / `local` / `collab` / `upstream`) when that role initiates a cross-agent change — worker-to-main report, main-to-worker delegate, EG-to-upstream report, upstream-to-downstream steering all follow the same rule. **Composition with existing §13.x — no override of orthogonal gates**: §13.14 redaction still gates the message *content* (placeholder substitution, technical-only phrasing); §13.17 main-chat ban still gates the message *destination* (board-mediated route for structured Q/A); §13.20 `BlockerManifest` emission is itself an A2A communication and gets the same priority; destructive-operation authorization gates are not bypassed when the prerequisite work is itself destructive. **Composition with §13.16.6** turn-end / next-cycle ritual: cursor-tail probe (element 1) and next-cycle rearm (element 2, relocated to next-cycle start in v2.4.9) run on their own schedule and are independent of this discipline — the priority rule governs new outbound messages triggered by the current cycle's work plan, not the liveness-maintenance loop. Element 5 (planned-queue scan) interacts in the obvious way: when the scan classifies the next progressable item as an outbound A2A message (or as prerequisite work for one), the priority rule confirms it as head-of-queue. **Composition with §13.18 recommend+proceed**: this priority rule sits above §13.18 — even a 1-line "recommend+proceed" announcement is itself an outbound message in the main-chat surface; if its emission unblocks a counterpart (a `Status` update the counterpart's `ReviewSLAAck` was waiting on, a board-side `Decision` downstream agents will read), the 1-line emission takes priority over other planned actions per the same drift-containment + counterpart-start-time rationales. **Failure mode this prevents**: 5-action plan with action #3 = `Delegate` to worker executed in plan-order delays the worker's start by the wall-clock cost of actions 1-2 and risks stale-state work if action 2 touched a spec the worker reads; the priority rule reorders to prerequisite-of-3 → 3 → (1, 2, 4, 5 in natural order), giving the same final state with counterpart starting at the earliest possible moment and drift bounded by round-trip latency. **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.9** (2026-06-01) — **`Constellation.md §13.16.6` element-ordering refinement: watcher rearm (element 2) relocates from turn-end to next-cycle start.** Constellation-only patch (frontmatter version v2.3.2 → v2.3.3). The 6-element turn-end ritual composition is unchanged in scope; what changes is the execution point of element 2 (unconditional watcher rearm). Element 2 now executes as the **first action at the start of the next user-facing response** (cycle N+1's start), not at the close of the current response (cycle N's turn-end). Elements 1 (cursor-tail probe), 3 (board-state real-time update), 4 (BOARD_STALE gate handoff), 5 (planned-queue scan), and 6 (pre-large-work context materialization) continue to execute at turn-end. The mandatory-order constraint (element 1 strictly before element 2) still holds and now spans the cycle-N→cycle-N+1 turn boundary. **Technical rationale**: (a) **concurrent-watcher-overlap avoidance** — running element 2 at turn-end of cycle N while the prior cycle's watcher may still be polling produces two watchers armed at near-identical `base` cursors covering the same forward window; the same-turn rearm does not add coverage (both share the armed-window blind spot) but does add a redundant concurrent watcher. Relocating to next-cycle start spawns exactly one watcher at a time across turn boundaries — the prior watcher has either WAKE'd or REARM-timed-out by cycle N+1's start, so the next-cycle-start spawn replaces rather than overlaps. (b) **Cleaner base-cursor semantics** — element 1 at turn-end of cycle N advances the agent's cursor to include any inbound below the prior watcher's `base`; if element 2 also ran at turn-end of cycle N, its fresh watcher's `base` would still miss any inbound that arrives between probe-time and final-text-emission. Relocating element 2 to next-cycle start means the rearm `base` is the line count at cycle-N+1-start, which by construction already includes any inbound the cycle-N+1-start re-probe just surfaced; the rearm-base invariant becomes "cursor-after-latest-processed-inbound" rather than "cursor-at-an-arbitrary-mid-turn-moment". **Net effect**: same coverage with one watcher armed at a time across turn boundaries, cleaner base-cursor invariant. **What didn't change**: all other turn-end ritual elements stay at turn-end; the cost-asymmetry argument for unconditional spawn discipline still holds; element 1 strictly before element 2 still holds. Edits to `Constellation.md §13.16.6`: frontmatter version bump, new "Element 2 timing — relocated from turn-end to next-cycle start" paragraph, "Mandatory ordering" paragraph's 4-step list relabeled with `[at turn-end of cycle N]` / `[at next-cycle start of cycle N+1, as the first action]` annotations, "Wrong order — anti-pattern" paragraph cross-references the relocation, "Composition with the other four elements" paragraph updated. **Scope discipline**: Constellation-only patch. Seed lib unchanged (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Protocol wire unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — in-flight patch tag cut, not catch-up.
- **v2.4.7** (2026-06-01) — **A2A PR System RRP v0.1 draft publish.** New RRP doc `constellation/reference/docs/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` (~55KB · 15 sections + headmatter) drafts a new Constellation protocol feature §13.22 — cross-repo Pull Request orchestration via the A2A messaging layer, replacing the manual hand-create-PR coordination tax that scales badly as cross-repo spec parity needs grow. **Wire vocabulary**: 5 new `CUSTOM` types — `PRRequest` / `PRDraftReady` / `PRReviewAck` / `PRMergeRequest`+`PRMergeAck` / `PRStatusUpdate`. **Agent topology**: 3 options evaluated (dedicated PR-bot agent / local-bridge `cmd:createPR(spec)` / hybrid) — recommendation: topology (b) local-bridge for v0.1 (reuse local git/gh CLI auth, no separate credential store). **Approval discipline**: 3 categories — `trusted_mirror` (state.json opt-in list) / `standard` (per-PR opt-in default) / `emergency` (block, never auto). **Content sourcing**: α (diff in payload) / β (branch ref + git API read) / γ (fork-based) — recommendation: β with α fallback for small diffs. **Authority**: §13.20 permission table extension — `role==main` for target repo can `PRMergeRequest`; any agent can `PRReviewAck`; `PRRequest` open. **State machine**: 5-state PR lifecycle (DRAFT → OPEN → IN_REVIEW → APPROVED → MERGED + side paths CLOSED / CHANGES_REQUESTED) + §13.19 deadlock integration (PR waiting >SLA on review = quasi-deadlock candidate) + live-board panel ask (PR queue visualization). **Dogfood plan**: canonical first use case = §13.14/§13.15 mirror PR from EG → `<hub-repo>` WS-PROTOCOL.md — the §13.14/§13.15 mirror PR itself is proposed as the first PR routed through the new system, proving the protocol works at the moment it lands. **Open questions × 8** (3 priority-flagged): topology — does `<hub-repo>` accept PRs via local `gh` CLI identity? content-sourcing — direct `mirror/...` branch push or fork-based? authority model — strict `role==main` gate or delegate to provider ACL? **Acceptance criteria**: spec (§13.22 body) · impl (local-bridge `createPR` cmd) · dogfood (§13.14/§13.15 mirror PR created via protocol, not manual) · composition (§13.19 + §13.20 integration). **Migration path**: phase 0 RRP review → phase 1 prototype → phase 2 dedicated PR-bot agent → phase 3 full §13.20 integration. **Redaction**: per §13.14, `<hub-repo>` / `<main-prod>` placeholders throughout; only `SoliEstre/EstreGenesis` (public repo) named directly. **Scope**: RRP-only draft — review-only artifact pending main review. v0.1 DRAFT status banner + every concrete design decision flagged "(open for main review)". Constellation.md §13.22 body integration is the post-review patch. Seed lib unchanged. Per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` 자체 태그 cut.

- **v2.4.3** (2026-05-31) — **DB P2 EG-side guide published — `constellation/reference/docs/DB-P2-Guide.md` (33KB · 11 sections + 7 open questions).** Per main upstream Delegate seq 144 (msgId m-mptlrmm3-143) — main DB P1 ship (5cd7fca: HistoryStore + JsonlStore wrapping current JSONL) entering P2 (SqliteStore via node:sqlite primary + better-sqlite3 fallback + dual-write + count reconciliation + bootstrap opt-in). EG responsibility per seq 79 DB RRP: discipline + gate + migration + rollback guide; main implements server.cjs. Guide structure: migration mode chain (A jsonl-only → B dual-write transitional → C db-primary terminal) · node:sqlite probe + better-sqlite3 fallback (Node 22.5+ + `--experimental-sqlite` flag check) · dual-write backfill (one-shot mode-B entry, idempotent `INSERT OR IGNORE`, batched transactions) · count-reconciliation gate (mismatch = abort B→C promotion + diff report, no auto-resolve) · bootstrap opt-in (default mode A on fresh install, operator-flipped via `state.json.modes.historyBackend`) · failure modes + recovery (WAL corruption, partial dual-write, count drift, BlockerManifest emission per §13.20) · schema sketch (1:1 JSONL field shape mirror) · `exportJsonl()` round-trip safety net · cross-links (§13.20, §13.19.4, P1 5cd7fca). 7 open questions: WAL checkpoint cadence · old JSONL retention policy · schema migration discipline for future versions · multi-server/replica story (out of scope) · `exportJsonl()` performance at 10^7+ · `source` column enum extensibility · backend probe cross-compatibility in mixed-Node deployments. Constellation.md unchanged; seed lib unchanged. Independent track per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` — Constellation-reference-doc-only patch cuts a tag of its own. §13.20 BlockerManifest list: 6 → 4 (this commit closes DB-P2-guide blocker; remaining: a5bc §F · Fix 2 PR · WS-PROTOCOL §13.14/§13.15 mirror PR · per-user/EG steering).
- **v2.4.2** (2026-05-31) — **§13.16.6 Filter discipline expanded: server-replay noise (`History`) + transport-layer acks added to the blocklist.** Constellation-only patch (seed lib version unchanged at v2.4.1). The v2.4.0 filter discipline scoped to `ev:"inbound"` to exclude self-emission echo (false-positive #1); v2.4.2 adds a second false-positive class — `History` payloads (server-side session replay on reconnect; line-level large, contains nested `Delegate`/`WorkerReport` events from prior sessions that a naive name-grep treats as fresh inbound) + transport-layer `Ack`/`AckProcessed`/`AckCumulative`/`AckPolicyUpdate` frames. Canonical bash filter is now two-stage: (1) `grep '"ev":"inbound"'` → (2) `grep -vE '"name":"(History|Ack|AckProcessed|AckCumulative|AckPolicyUpdate|ServerNotice|AgentList|Status|ConnectionRestored|Heartbeat|Typing|UserPromptAccepted|PersistentAdapterSmoke|OnboardAck|WorkerInboxReceived|EditMessage|MainChanged)"'` → (3) `grep -cE '"name":"(Delegate|UserPrompt|WorkerReport|WorkerAck|AgentHello|Handoff|Report|Command)"'`. Surfacing incident: watcher `bbae2ph8r` 2026-05-31 wake caught a server `History` replay payload as a `WAKE (meaningful)` event — historical inbound from prior sessions matched by name-only grep, not a new external delivery. Constellation.md §13.16.6 Filter-discipline paragraph rewritten end-to-end; no seed body change required (seeds reference §13.16.6 by anchor, not by body). Cadence: per `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md`, cut a Constellation-only patch tag immediately rather than rolling into the next seed-lib release.
- **v2.4.1** (2026-05-31) — **§13.16.6 element-ordering reinforcement: cursor-tail probe MUST execute BEFORE unconditional rearm.** Discipline-tightening patch. The 6-element turn-end ritual composition is unchanged; what was missing is the mandatory ordering between element 1 (inbox cursor-tail probe) and element 2 (unconditional rearm). Probe is reframed from "telemetry only, never a gate" (v2.4.0 wording) to **PRIMARY catch** for the armed-window blind spot — rearm alone does NOT recover inbound below its own base. Explicit 4-step ordered sequence added: (a) tail inbox.log from last-surfaced cursor → (b) surface any meaningful inbound → (c) advance cursor → (d) THEN unconditional rearm. Anti-pattern paragraph added with 2026-05-31 incident anchor: agent ran rearm first, missed seq 123 (Status) + seq 127 (Report: main DB P1 ship `5cd7fca` + §13.19 P2 spec-delivery query) from the prior watcher's SIGSTOP-suspend window; user surfaced "메인이 회신 대기중이라는데" to force the cursor-tail probe that should have run at turn-end automatically. Composition paragraph updated to call out element 1 as PRIMARY (armed-window blind-spot catch) + element 2 as forward-looking (next-idle-window catch); BOARD_STALE gate downgraded from "safety net" to "fail-safe / backstop when agent-side discipline fails". Cascade across `Constellation.md §13.16.6` + seed × 6 (Master / Lite / Compact × EN/KO) with the established verbosity gradient. First test-drive of the `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` policy (cut versions in flight, not batch catch-ups) — v2.4.0 was the long-overdue catch-up; v2.4.1 lands the same day for a single discipline-tightening change.
- **v2.4.0** (2026-05-31) — **Constellation coordination-layer protocol expansion: §13.16.6 absolute turn-end ritual (6 elements) + §13.16.7 BOARD_STALE + §13.17 main-chat ban + §13.18 recommend+proceed + §13.19 deadlock formal spec + §13.20 blocker tracking + §13.21 fresh-context defer anti-pattern; `.eux` v1 spec publish + UI 6 / KEY-MGMT WS protocol drafts; EstreUX seed × 6 cascade (option C closed); reference sync to main UI 3·4·5·6 ship.** Seven new/revised `§13.x` Constellation sub-sections form a continuous autonomous-execution discipline chain. (1) **§13.16.6 v2** — turn-end mandatory ritual escalated to absolute-tier 6-element checklist: inbox.log cursor-tail probe · UNCONDITIONAL watcher rearm (probe is telemetry, never a gate; cost-asymmetry argument FP-spawn-harmless < FN-miss-silent-stall; conditional rearm from earlier draft RETIRED) · board state real-time update · BOARD_STALE gate · **planned-queue scan (#442)** · **pre-large-work context materialization** (durable artifact emit so post-compact resume is possible). Watcher liveness probe + cursor-tail fix + 4-evidence-confirmed armed-window-blind-spot diagnosis + bg-task SIGSTOP wall-clock-vs-task-clock observation + filter-discipline self-emission exclusion. (2) **§13.16.7 BOARD_STALE gate** — pre-rearm board freshness check via `git log -1 HEAD --format=%ct > git log -1 -- state.json --format=%ct` (identity-based; an earlier 120s time-buffer version self-trapped and is retired). (3) **§13.17 main-chat structured-choice prompts FORBIDDEN** — `AskUserQuestion`-style option UI bans in agent main-chat (no board projection); route via `defer-OK` review-items tab or `need-now` UI6; review-items tab badge "0 → hidden, tab stays" UX discipline. (4) **§13.18 non-branching choices recommend+proceed** — when a recommendation exists for a non-fork-of-architecture choice, 1-line announce + proceed; do NOT escalate via `A/B/C/D?` list; parallel is default-presumption when feasible. (5) **§13.19 deadlock formal spec** — wait-pattern classification (strict / quasi / healthy + livelock=quasi variant) · detection (wait-edge DFS 2-agent + wait-class timeouts + §13.16.6 agent-active correction) · prevention (priority ordering §13.9 tree + `ReviewSLAAck{eta,SLA-OR-WORK}` + termination signals `DONE / BLOCKED{reason,waitingOn} / NEEDS_HUMAN`) · auto-resolution (preemption `PreemptRequest/Force` + deadline + starvation guard) · escalation 4-tier (ordering → preemption → mediation → human §13.17) · 3-tier ack layering above §13.13 (transport / commitment / application). Q2-Q3-Q4-Q6 decisions: CNP rejected-as-wire + preserved-as-discipline; mediator hybrid (board adapter default + 3rd-party agent opt-in); human-fallback bounded-probe-count × wait-class severity, cap ~3-5/24h; renegotiate-SLA fixed cap N=2 then human-escalate. (6) **§13.20 blocker tracking + periodic nudge discipline** — `BlockerManifest` emit BEFORE idle wait (subject / reason / EG-side action / request-history + count); periodic `BlockerNudge` (env `CONSTELLATION_BLOCKER_NUDGE_CYCLES`, default 1 per ~45min rearm); 4-tier escalation polite → explicit + ETA → hard deadline → human §13.17; distinct from §13.19 (linear-stalled blocker vs cyclic-deadlock). Live-board panel ask to main upstream (external-blocker-manifest visualization). (7) **§13.21 fresh-context defer = anti-pattern** — compact is harness-fired on threshold (no agent `/compact` discretion); fresh-context expectation is wishful + unrealistic; planned MUST NOT be deferred under context-length excuses (#442 reinforcement: time + context excuses both forbidden). The §13.16.6 element 6 is the *capability* (materialize artifacts), §13.21 is the *discipline* (defer forbidden). Three-section policy chain ships: §13.18 (choice-surface) → §13.16.6 #442 + element 6 (work-progress-surface) → §13.21 (time-surface). **`.eux` format v1**: `constellation/reference/docs/eux-format-v1.md` (26.9KB · 9 directives total: 5 formal/tier-gated + 4 structural; v0's 8 + new `@behavior`; `@deps` absorbed under `@ports.deps` per RRP A4 amendment per 12-file EG empirical evidence); `EUX-V1-CATALOG.md` (291 lines — profile distribution, per-file matrix, Verify "runtime 6-check matrix" with C1-C6 prefix to disambiguate from spec §4 G1-G6 structural gates); `WS-PROTOCOL-KEY-MGMT.md` (22KB · 5 message types `KeyIssue/KeyList/KeyRevoke[immediate|sessionEnd]/KeyLabel/AgentNameChanged` + 5-state machine + role-naming align `main|local|collab|upstream`); `WS-PROTOCOL-UI6-SELECTION.md` (25.8KB · 3 message types `SelectionPrompt/Answer/Cancel` + 3-state machine; cohesion-separated from KEY-MGMT). **EstreUX seed × 6 cascade** closes long-deferred option C: `§5 #12 EstreUX adoption + citation` core rule + `§ Constellation → ### EstreUX (Estre Universal eXpression)` sub-section across Master EN/KO + Lite EN/KO + Compact EN/KO with tier verbosity gradient. **Runtime updates**: `self-wake-watcher` poll interval 15s → 5s (`MAX 196 → 588`, ~49min rearm preserved); `ws-core.eux` v0.2 fragmented frame assembly (FIN-bit + `_frag` accumulator + `_deliver` single entry, `conn.remoteAddr`/`conn.ua` ports); anonymous-HELLO reject (`conn.meta.anonymous` flag + origin logging + relay-skip); pre-commit `check-reference-syntax.mjs` syntax gate + `check-reference-regressions.mjs` proposal-002/004 functional guard; `local-ide-agent` legacy-identifier sweep → generic `main-agent` per §13.14 redaction. **Reference sync** to main UI 3·4·5·6 ship (521+ insertions): KEY-MGMT legacy `RegisterUpstreamKey` reconciliation (supersede + transitional alias, deprecated v0.2, retire on zero-traffic gate); ---

<a id="한국어"></a>

## 변경 이력 (한국어)

각 tier 는 자체 버전 보유. 마스터가 권위 있는 진화 트랙; Lite·Compact 는 정기적으로 마스터에서 파생되나 한 릴리스 지연될 수 있음.

본 파일이 **changelog SSoT** — 각 시드 파일은 tier, 언어, 현재 버전, counterpart, 그리고 시드를 복사한 대상 프로젝트의 README가 아닌 본 `CHANGELOG.md` 포인터만 담은 짧은 헤더 메타데이터를 유지. 마이그레이션 B 로 프로젝트 업그레이드 시 에이전트는 시드 헤더의 버전 마커와 본 changelog 로 delta 를 계산.

- **v1.0** (2026-04-18) — 초판 (마스터). Author의 두 번째 AI Native 프로젝트 기반.
- **v1.1** (2026-04-19) — Research → Report → Plan 루프 섹션 추가. 핵심 원칙 #7.
- **v1.2** (2026-04-20) — 마이그레이션 A/B/C 가이드 추가. 에이전트 지침 상단 Bootstrap/Migration 모드 분기. Lite·Compact tier 초판 릴리스.
- **v1.3** (2026-05-02) — 핵심 원칙 2개 추가: #8 (인덱스 ↔ 본문 동기화) · #9 (외부 인터페이스 N-way sync). 신설 섹션 6개: § 인덱스 동기화 정책 · § 외부 인터페이스 N-way sync · § 마크다운 `~` escape 정책 · § RAG 인덱스 최적화 · § 외부 전달용 빌드 파이프라인 · § 문서 인플레이션 방지 (부록 `<NN>b_*.md` 패턴). 3 tier 모두 업데이트; Lite·Compact 는 동일 패턴의 축약본 추가. 모든 추가는 Author의 두 번째 AI Native 프로젝트의 2026-04-21 → 2026-05-02 운영 실측 사례에서 추출: 외부 표면이 일주일 stale 상태로 누락됨 (N-way sync 정책 동기), 외부 송부용 PDF 의 마지막-순간 마크다운 취소선 오작동 (tilde escape 정책 동기), 다른 에이전트가 옛 인덱스로 작업 (인덱스 동기화 정책 동기), Claude 프로젝트 워크스페이스의 파일 용량 100% 도달 (RAG 친화 인덱스 규칙 동기).
- **v1.3.1** (2026-05-02) — 자기 완결 툴링: 마스터 시드 § 파일 템플릿이 외부 송부용 툴체인 전체 inline 스크립트를 내장 — 시드만 가지고 전체 부트스트랩 가능. 신설 템플릿: `scripts/escape-md-tildes.mjs` (의존 없는 Node ≥18, idempotent, placeholder 보호 알고리즘), `scripts/build-md-to-html.mjs` (`marked` 기반 MD → A4 HTML + h2 page-break + 프로젝트 언어 폰트 스택), 편의 wrapper `scripts/build-pdf.ps1` (Windows) / `scripts/build-pdf.sh` (macOS/Linux) — 3 단계 `escape → HTML → Chrome --print-to-pdf` 파이프라인 chain. § 마크다운 `~` escape 정책에 "알고리즘" 서브섹션 추가 (placeholder 보호가 *왜* 필수인지 — 순진한 regex 의 함정). § 외부 전달용 빌드 파이프라인에 "왜 이 도구들인가" 서브섹션 (`marked` vs Puppeteer trade-off, A4 page rules) + macOS/Linux Chrome 등가물. Lite·Compact tier 의 § 마크다운 `~` escape (축약) 에 placeholder 알고리즘 요약과 크로스플랫폼 PDF 파이프라인 보강; 마스터 시드가 inline 스크립트의 단일 진실 원천 유지.
- **v1.3.2** (2026-05-02) — `.gitignore` 템플릿 + cross-tier 정합성 감사. **`.gitignore`**: 마스터 시드 § 파일 템플릿이 inline 템플릿 내장 — Common (OS, IDE, env, 로그) + Node / Python / Go / Rust / JVM / C-C++ / Mobile / DB 스택별 행 + 시드 산출물 블록 (`.generated.` infix 컨벤션 사용 — 빌드 산출물만 정확히 휩쓸고 수공 첨부는 보호). **Cross-tier 정합성 감사**: README 의 stated 원칙 ("각 tier 는 self-contained — 다른 tier 로의 forward/backward 참조 없음") 이 v1.0 부터 위반돼 왔고, v1.3.1 릴리스가 cross-tier 참조를 더 추가해 악화. v1.3.2 가 **Lite** 와 **Compact** tier 를 원칙 준수로 정상화 — 모든 "→ 마스터 시드 § ..." cross-reference 제거. Lite 는 909 / 912 줄 (한국어 / 영문) 에서 신설 § 파일 템플릿이 inline AGENTS.md, `.agent/rules.md`, `.gitignore` (Common + Phase 2 스택 + 시드 산출물), `scripts/escape-md-tildes.mjs` (압축 Node ≥18), `scripts/build-md-to-html.mjs` (압축 `marked` + A4 CSS), 11 종 지원 AI 서비스 브릿지 stub 모두 내장. Compact 는 119 줄/언어 에서 신설 § 스캐폴드 spec 가 각 스캐폴드 대상에 알고리즘-spec 묘사 — 에이전트가 spec 읽고 실제 파일 생성. 3 tier 모두 README 가 처음부터 약속해 온 *프로젝트 repo 에 독립 ship* 이제 준수.
- **v1.3.4** (2026-05-03) — 강제 훅 아키텍처 추가. Master 는 Layer 1 Claude Code `PreToolUse` + Layer 2 `git pre-commit` 2중 방어, 단일 regex SSoT `scripts/hooks/_patterns.mjs`, `.git/hooks/pre-commit` shim 및 `.claude/settings.local.json` 병합 installer, 경로 매칭·Bash 따옴표/HEREDOC false-positive 회피·테스트·cross-AI 적용 범위를 전체 섹션으로 설명. Lite 는 축약 섹션, Compact 는 원칙 #10 과 동기화 규칙 bullet 추가.
- **v1.3.5** (2026-05-03) — 작업 분해 전략 추가. 분해 경로가 여러 개인 복잡 작업에서 에이전트가 선택한 진행 형태를 announce 하고, 판단/관성에 따라 확인 대기 없이 진행하며, 사용자 피벗을 즉시 반영하는 cross-AI 행동 패턴을 추가. Master 는 임계값·관성 우선순위·AI 별 도구 매핑·안티패턴을 포함하고, Lite·Compact 는 축약 형태로 반영.
- **v1.3.6** (2026-05-03) — 인덱스 ↔ 본문 동기화에 외부 지식 인덱스 자동 동기화 추가. 프로젝트가 Claude 메모리·Notion·wiki·RAG 메타데이터 같은 외부 KB 에 구조화 폴더를 미러링하면, pre-commit 이 전용 sync 스크립트로 메커니컬 구조(카운트·stub·번호·orphan 경고)를 자동 갱신하고 의미 콘텐츠는 사람 큐레이션으로 유지. Master 는 전체 subsection, Lite·Compact 는 축약 절 반영.
- **v1.3.7** (2026-05-03) — Phase 0 이 작업 언어 다음에 에이전트 응답 말투를 선택하도록 확장. 한국어 프롬프트는 `~니다`, `~에요/예요/어요`, `~음/슴/임`, 친구/동료 말투, 직설 도전 말투, 직접 방향성 프롬프트 6가지를 제시하고, 영문 프롬프트는 이에 부합하는 tone 옵션을 제공. 기본값은 사용자가 대화를 건 톤과 동일하거나 한 단계 공손하게. 생성되는 `AGENTS.md`, `.agent/rules.md`, 브릿지 stub 이 언어와 말투를 분리 기록.
- **v1.4.0** (2026-05-03) — 문서 제목 전반에 EstreGenesis 정식 네이밍 적용, 소스 프로젝트 참조 공개용 익명화, public repo 공개. 콘텐츠 베이스: legacy private archive, commit `5944a50` (v1.3.6, 2026-05-03).
- **v1.4.1** (2026-05-06) — 메타데이터 정합화. v1.3.6 → v1.4.0 흡수 과정에서 Master tier (KO/EN) 의 마이그레이션 B delta 표에 v1.3.4 (강제 훅 아키텍처) · v1.3.5 (작업 분해 전략) · v1.3.6 (외부 지식 인덱스 자동 동기화) 행이 누락 — 다른 4 tier 는 정상 보유. v1.4.0 콘텐츠는 그대로 유지하고 누락된 3 행만 보강해 6-tier sync 복원. Master 의 Phase 7 § 파일 스캐폴딩 체크리스트에 옵션 `scripts/hooks/` 블록 명시 (강제 훅 아키텍처는 절대 규칙 강제가 필요한 프로젝트의 opt-in). README v1.4.0 항목에 legacy archive SHA 박제 추가.
- **v1.5.0** (2026-05-07) — 6개 시드 파일 전체에 Bootstrap Residency 추가. 새 Phase 2.5 가 `<scope-root>` 선택 전 작업공간이 소스 repo, 개인 agent-docs sidecar, 다중 프로젝트 오케스트레이션 repo, upstream/local split 중 무엇인지 결정. Minimal, Full manual, repo-provider assisted bootstrap 지원 (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Azure DevOps, Gitea, Forgejo, self-hosted/local remotes, 사용자 제공 repo 목록), workspace-limited agent 안내, upstream 폴더 기본값 `upstream/` 및 사용자 지정명 허용, sidecar 소스 폴더 `.gitignore` 등록은 사용자 식별 + 에이전트 확인 후로 제한. Master 는 트리거 조건이 있는 Adoption Catalog 를 추가하고 Lite·Compact 는 축약 반영.
- **v1.5.1** (2026-05-08) — 적용 프로젝트 피드백 기반 패치 릴리스. 6개 시드 헤더 모두에서 changelog 포인터가 시드를 복사한 대상 프로젝트의 README.md가 아니라 **upstream EstreGenesis repository README.md** 를 뜻한다고 명시. KO Master 는 v1.5.0 흡수 잔여 결함도 보정: Phase 0·Phase 4 마무리 줄을 Phase 7로 정정, 신규 Phase 2.5 sub-heading 한국어화, Adoption Catalog 제목/표 헤더 한국어화.
- **v1.6.0** (2026-05-09) — Agent-time vs human-time 추정. AI 에이전트가 인간 dev 팀 baseline 으로 추정하면 plan 이 5\~10× 부풀어 calendar mismatch 발생하고 PM 템플릿이 현실을 잘못 묘사. Phase 0 가 언어·말투 다음에 한 가지 더 묻도록 확장 — **실행 페이스 모드**: Cautious 2\~4× (무료 티어 또는 Continue.dev·로컬 모델 사용 Aider 같은 로컬 LLM, 출력 토큰/초 기준 추가 보정), Proactive 5\~6× (유료 플랜 기본값), Burst 6\~8× (고처리량 플랜), Sprint 9\~10× (사실상 무제한 토큰, 최대 병렬화). 각 모드 안에서 작업 유형이 위치 조정 — 실행 중심은 상단, 디버깅은 중간, 연구·전략은 인간 검토가 율속이라 모드 무관 ~1×. 모든 duration 추정은 **agent active time** 과 **human review / approval time** 분리 + handoff 갭 흡수하는 **calendar window**. 모드는 프로젝트 단위지만 진행 중 전환 가능 ("switch to sprint" / "drop to cautious") — 활성 PM 추정치 재산정 + CHANGELOG 기록 자동. `.agent/_lessons/` 자가 보정: ±30% 초과 delta 만 `estimation` 태그로 기록, 같은 모드에서 3개+ 누적 시 보정 multiplier 제안. Master 는 핵심 원칙 #11 + § Agent-Time 추정 정책 섹션 풀버전 (2축 프레임워크, 모드 전환 프로토콜, 자가 보정 루프, 안티패턴, cross-AI 적용성). Lite 는 원칙 #8 + 축약 정책 섹션. Compact 는 원칙 #13 인라인. PM 템플릿은 모든 tier 에서 split-time 형식으로 갱신. AGENTS.md 핵심 규칙 라인 1 이 언어 + 말투 + 페이스 모드 함께 기록.
- **v2.0.0** (2026-05-27) — **Constellation** 추가 (핵심원칙 #12 / Lite #9 / Compact #14), 선택적 모듈 하나. 멀티에이전트 코디네이션을 파일 기반 `.agent/_coordination/` 에서 실시간 라이브보드(WebSocket + A2A 메시징 + 대시보드)로 격상. **A2A 브릿지 인터페이스** (role board/main/local/upstream/collab · 핸드셰이크 · 메시징 · turn 기반 브릿지 데몬 + self-wake watcher 런타임 패턴) 가 불변 계약; 도입 깊이는 시드 티어 따라감. 별도 `Constellation.md` 가이드 + `constellation/*.eux` 컴포넌트 spec (`gateway-client.eux` = 디테일 티어 A2A 어댑터 포함) 으로 ship, tier 시드는 raw GitHub URL 로 참조해 lean 유지. 라이브보드 UI 컴포넌트는 `.eux` 로 작성해 **EstreUX** 로 brew — EstreUX 는 EstreGenesis 가 *참조*하는 별도 런타임(번들·소유 X); EstreGenesis 는 EUX 포맷을 소유·교육하지 않음 — EUX 는 Constellation 의 빌드타임 의존이지 시드의 레이어가 아님. 파일 기반 코디네이션(Phase 5)이 기본. 이전 v1.6.0 상태는 `1.x` 브랜치 보존; 2.0 은 `main`. Constellation 은 공개 EstreGenesis Claude 플러그인으로 성숙해 감.
- **v2.1.0** (2026-05-28) — **Constellation 런타임 증류 + 자족화.** 라이브보드 런타임을 공개 `.eux` 로 증류해 비공개 레퍼런스 런타임 접근 없이도 호환 보드를 구현 가능: `constellation/server.eux` (deps-0 HTTP + WS 라우터 — 에이전트 레지스트리, role 분류, A2A relay + reply-window 페어링, telemetry 제외, graceful main 핸드오프, 채널별 history), `local-bridge.eux` (turn 기반 에이전트용 파일-IO control/A2A 브릿지), `self-wake-watcher.eux` (무한대기 self-wake), `watchdog.eux` (server/bridge liveness 가드). `Constellation.md` 를 **자족화** — 오케스트레이션 프로토콜 + 무한대기 방법론을 본문 증류(A2A reply-envelope, telemetry 제외, 핸드셰이크 순서), 비공개 파일 인용 제거, **watch-state 불변식**(보드 합류 중엔 대화를 끝내지 않음 — 항상 watcher 재무장 후 watch 복귀) + re-arm duty + watch 규율 강화. **EstreUX brew 런타임 참조** 를 끝까지 명확화: repo URL + clone-and-run brew CLI(`node bin/estreux.mjs brew`) 를 `Constellation.md §6` 와 `constellation/README.md` 에 추가(비공개 레퍼런스 클라 인용 대체), EstreUX 한 줄 포인터를 6개 시드 티어 전체에 propagate 해 마이그레이션 에이전트가 런타임을 찾을 수 있게. EstreUX 는 참조 Apache-2.0 빌드 의존으로 유지(번들·소유 X). draft 는 EstreGenesis 에이전트가 디스크 런타임 소스에서 증류하고 upstream 라이브보드 메인이 정밀 review.
- **v2.1.1** (2026-05-28) — EstreUX brew 런타임 참조 동기화. EstreUX 가 `v0.1.0` 발행(deps-0 ~21 KB 엔진, files 화이트리스트)되어, v2.1.0 의 "clone-and-run, npm 아님" 문구를 권장 경량 **giget** fetch(`npx giget gh:SoliEstre/EstreUX/spike#v0.1.0 ./estreux-engine` → `node ./estreux-engine/expand.mjs brew <comp>.eux`)로 갱신하고 full-clone(`bin/estreux.mjs`)·npm 발행 준비본을 대안으로 명기. `Constellation.md §6`·`constellation/README.md`·시드 6종 EstreUX 포인터에 반영, Compact 티어 EstreUX 중복 표현 정리.
- **v2.2.0** (2026-05-28) — **Constellation reference 마스터 copy.** rough/detail `.eux` spec 옆에 풀세트 기준이 필요한 다운스트림용으로 `constellation/reference/` 신설: `state-schema.md` (보드 SSoT 데이터 모델 — `state.json` top-level + 작업 트랙 `current/done/planned` + 검토·결정 패널 + 자유 추가 요청 + 채널별 history + 키 + 피드백, generic-PM vs 도메인-특수 경계 명시)과 `dashboard/` (`index.html`·`style.css`·`app.js` 비공개 구현에서 일반화한 vanilla DOM 마스터 copy, schema 기준 `state.json` 렌더; copy해서 stack에 맞게 re-skin). §2 A2A 브릿지 인터페이스만 byte-identical 불변; reference copy는 구체 출발점이지 계약 아님. `gateway/`·`runtime/` reference 마스터 copy는 post-v2.2.0 patch 예정(주기적 재증류로 drift 관리). rough tier brew 결과가 ping/pong 수준 보드만 만든 다운스트림 마이그레이션 사례로부터 진단 — 갭은 "무엇을 렌더할까?"(데이터 모델)지 "어떻게 렌더할까?"(UI 디자인) 아니었음. EstreGenesis 에이전트 draft, upstream 라이브보드 메인 정밀 review.
- **v2.3.0** (2026-05-29) — **Superscalar 모듈 + 자율 실행 절대 원칙.** 핵심 원칙 2개 신규 추가 (Master #13/#14, Lite #10/#11, Compact #15/#16): (1) **실행 스케줄링 (Superscalar, 선택 참조 모듈)** — `issue_width`를 5개 차원(Anthropic effort band · pace_mode 상한 · Little's Law throughput · Kanban WIP · `autonomy_available_workers`)으로 제한, cost-benefit 게이트(~30-60k 토큰 지평 crossover) 통과 시 dispatch; (2) **자율 실행 (절대)** — 정해진-다음-단계(Phase 순서 · `planned` 트랙 · `blocked` 해제분 · in-order retire 큐)는 묻지 말고 진행, 게이트는 오직 (a) 손실 / 외부 발행, (b) 새 중대 분기 결정 시점 (RRP / 설계 — *결정 시점* 만; 그 결과로 잡힌 Phase A/B/C 계획은 *결정된 실행*), (c) 재기동 필요 deploy (적용은 자율, *재기동 타이밍* 만 조율), (d) 명시적 사용자 steering. Phase 0에 네 번째 질문 추가 (`실행 스케줄링: serial/parallel` + `speculation: off/on`); AGENTS.md template § 5 핵심 규칙 라인 1이 자율 실행 규칙으로 정합. Master는 § 실행 스케줄링 신규 섹션 추가하여 `Superscalar.md` 참조 (§ Constellation과 동일 모듈-참조 패턴); Lite/Compact는 원칙 안 압축 참조. v2.2.x patch 시리즈를 한 anchor로 통합: **v2.2.1** (Hermes gateway reference 마스터 copy), **v2.2.2** (`constellation/reference/gateway/main` + `runtime/` references — Node deps-0 generic adapter), **v2.2.3** (upstream 라이브보드 Report 2 fixes — A2A classifier · `AgentHello` shape literal · cursor unit drift), **v2.2.4** (Report 2 follow-up — server-stamped truth · leniency-WARN · role hint vs truth · runtime liveness). Superscalar Stage 1 dogfood baseline (`Superscalar.md §11` Entry 01-03, Phase C reference 작업) 안정 ship; `autonomy_available_workers` 차원과 Andon 워커-오토모드 precheck는 dogfood telemetry(Haiku-tier 워커가 자율 lane에 부적합 — 매 dispatch마다 권한 창이 throughput 무너뜨림)로부터 추가. EstreGenesis 에이전트가 draft하고 upstream 라이브보드 메인 협업 review (Delegate seq 119 dogfood telemetry + seq 123 절대 원칙 박기).

- **v2.5.35** (2026-06-03) — **시드 lib v2.4.1 → v2.4.2 — 마이그레이션 B dual-track guidance per bundle 007 M1: Step 1 (시작 버전 파악) + Step 2 (역량 차이 산출) 가 이제 seed-version vs EG-release-version 분리를 explicit 설명하고 시작 상태 선언 전에 두 마커 모두 cross-check 요구. 6 시드 tier 전반 (Master + Lite + Compact × EN/KO) cascade.** 시드-lib cut. Bundle 007 M1 가 2-트랙 추적 갭 surface: seed-version 마커 (예: `v2.4.1`, `AGENTS.md` embedded) 와 EG-release version (예: `v2.5.x`, `feedback_release_versioning_cadence.md` 정합 의미있는 push 마다 advance) 가 독립적 — release-only cut (예: Constellation `§13.x` patch, Hyperbrief 모듈 ship) 은 seed version bump 안 함, 그래서 seed 마커만 확인하는 마이그레이션 어댑터가 substantial module/spec 변경이 landed 됐음에도 "delta 없음" 판단 위험. 수정은 마이그레이션 B Step 1 + Step 2 재작성 (Master tier full, Lite tier condensed, Compact tier 1-liner) 으로 dual-track 기대를 explicit. **Master tier (Master EN + Master KO)** — Step 1 이 한 단락에서 두 트랙 ("seed version" vs "EG release version") 을 명명하는 구조적 sub-section + 실패 모드 설명 "Check both markers before declaring a starting version" + cross-check sources (AGENTS.md seed 마커 + adoption manifest EG-release + upstream `CHANGELOG.md` HEAD) + revised user-question wording ("which EG release tag was current at that time?") 로 확장. Step 2 이 "List X for the starting **seed version** (table below), AND list Y for the starting **release version** (consult upstream `CHANGELOG.md` between the two release tags — typically a `git log <starting-tag>..HEAD --oneline -- CHANGELOG.md` against the EG repo, or just read the CHANGELOG entries between the two tags)" 로 preface, 기존 seed-delta 표가 "Seed-delta table" 라벨로 reader가 두 트랙 중 하나일 뿐임을 인지. **Lite tier (Lite EN + Lite KO)** — condensed equivalent: Step 1 이 2문장으로 dual-track 설명 + cross-check 지시; Step 2 가 dual-track diff 로 preface. **Compact tier (Compact EN + Compact KO)** — Step 1 시작의 1-liner 확장 + Step 2 의 1-liner reframe ("역량 차이 산출 (두 트랙)"). **Frontmatter 버전 마커** — 6 tier header 모두 `version: v2.4.1 → v2.4.2` + `date: 2026-05-31 → 2026-06-03` + status fragment `v2.4.2 = bundle 007 M1 reflection — 마이그레이션 B Step 1/2 dual-track guidance` (Master) / condensed forms (Lite + Compact) bump. **시드 bump 인 이유 (단순 CHANGELOG note 가 아닌)** — 변경이 시드 body 자체 (마이그레이션 B 절차) 에 대한 것, 참조 모듈에 대한 것이 아님 — 본 시드 cut 으로 신규 프로젝트 부트스트랩하는 어댑터가 out-of-band CHANGELOG cross-reference 가 아닌 마이그레이션 B 섹션 내장 형태로 dual-track guidance 받음. seed-version 마커가 v2.4.1 (2026-05-31) 부터 변경 없었음 — 앞선 cuts (v2.5.0 ~ v2.5.34) 모두 시드 body 를 건드리지 않은 release-track 변경이었기 때문 — 본 cut 이 v2.4.1 이래 첫 진정한 seed-body 변경, 본 변경 자체가 codify 하는 2-트랙 분리를 validate. **Cross-tier 일관성 check 통과** — dual-track guidance 가 이제 6 tier 모두에 present; substance 동일 (두 트랙, 두 마커 cross-check, 사용자에게 그 시점의 EG release tag 질문); verbosity 가 tier 별로 scale (Master = full prose 설명, Lite = 2 문장, Compact = 1 line). **Scope 규율**: 6 시드 tier 파일 (Master EN + Master KO + Lite EN + Lite KO + Compact EN + Compact KO) — 각각 마이그레이션 B Step 1 + Step 2 prefix 갱신 + frontmatter 버전 bump. 모듈 변경 없음 (Constellation.md / Superscalar.md / Hyperbrief.md untouched). 플러그인 변경 없음. Hyperbrief는 묻는다: 이건 사용자 위임을 요구하는가?"); read-only lane을 Hyperbrief 구조적 면제로 명명(§3 irreversibility-barrier read/write 분리 상속); write/deploy/send lane을 gate-pass-then-hyperbrief-check로 명명(cost-benefit gate 먼저, 그 뒤 `hyperbrief-trigger-check`; AUTONOMOUS_DECIDE → lane이 one-line post-notify와 함께 진행; FULL_HYPERBRIEF → lane pause, Constellation `DECISION_REQUEST + HyperbriefCard` emit, `ack_tier='decided'` 대기, 가역적 sibling lane은 Superscalar latency-hiding 하에 계속); multi-lane batching 패턴 명명(n개 write/deploy/send lane이 모두 escalate하면 lane manifest의 `sibling_lanes` 필드를 통해 Hyperbrief가 sibling lane을 MCDA alternative row로 갖는 하나의 consolidated `HyperbriefCard` emit — n-card 결정 flood 방지); user-outcome routing 명명(accept → resume, defer → `defer_until` queue, reject_framing → cancel, request_investigation → research lane spawn); speculation 규율 명명(§4 speculative lane은 read-only / sandboxed-test 측에 머물러야 하므로 Hyperbrief gate에 도달 불가; speculative lane의 retire-time commit이 barrier를 cross한다면 그 commit이 side-effecting action이며 retire 시점에 gate 진입); 표준 pseudocode 포함; Hyperbrief.md §2(trigger rubric) + §9(Decision Capture feed-back) + Constellation.md §13.16.9(A2A intents + `ack_tier='decided'`) 교차 참조. **Superscalar.md frontmatter** `version: v0.4.0 → v0.4.1` + status string에 새 fragment 추가(`+ Hyperbrief decision-delegation interlock (v0.4.1 §3.1 — orthogonal gate, serial evaluation: write/deploy/send lanes pass through cost-benefit gate AND hyperbrief-trigger-check, read-only exempt)`) + `depends-on` 줄에 새 optional synergy 추가(`Hyperbrief §2 trigger rubric — both orthogonal`). **`plugins/superscalar/.claude-plugin/plugin.json`** version `0.1.0 → 0.1.1` + description이 v0.4 wrap을 v0.4.1로 확장 + §3.1 interlock 명명. **`plugins/superscalar/skills/superscalar/SKILL.md`** `description:`이 v0.4.1 §3.1 Hyperbrief-interlock 문장으로 확장되어 skill이 적절 시점에 cross-module check를 발동("for write/deploy/send lanes that pass the cost-benefit gate, also invoke `hyperbrief-trigger-check`; on FULL_HYPERBRIEF pause the lane and emit Constellation `DECISION_REQUEST + HyperbriefCard`, await `ack_tier='decided'`; read-only lanes are exempt by construction"). **`Hyperbrief.md §11.1 v0.3.0`**이 "queued"에서 "Superscalar v0.4.1(Superscalar.md §3.1 — 직교 게이트, 직렬 평가; cost-benefit gate를 통과한 write/deploy/send lane이 hyperbrief-trigger-check에 진입; read-only lane 면제; multi-lane batching이 sibling lane을 MCDA row로 갖는 단일 HyperbriefCard emit)에서 shipped. EG cut v2.5.29."로 재작성. Hyperbrief frontmatter `depends-on`이 Superscalar §3.1을 active로 표기하도록 갱신. **Cross-module 일관성**: Hyperbrief.md §9 Superscalar Integration sub-section은 이미 본 interlock 기준으로 작성됨; v2.5.29는 그 참조를 forward-pointing이 아닌 live로 만드는 Superscalar-side cascade. 두 모듈의 통합 pseudocode가 이제 일치(Hyperbrief.md §9와 Superscalar.md §3.1 양쪽이 동일한 lane-shape state machine 표현 — `cost_benefit_gate → trigger_check → FULL_HYPERBRIEF? → pause + emit + await tier=decided → switch user_outcome`). **Scope 규율**: `Superscalar.md` 의 spec-body 패치(§3.1 신규 sub-section + frontmatter version + status string + depends-on) + `Hyperbrief.md`(frontmatter depends-on + §11.1 v0.3.0 status) + `plugins/superscalar/.claude-plugin/plugin.json`의 plugin manifest 패치(version + description) + `plugins/superscalar/skills/superscalar/SKILL.md`(description 확장). Reference runtime 변경 없음. Schema 변경 없음. Renderer 변경 없음. MCP server 변경 없음. Constellation.md 변경 없음(§3.1의 cross-reference가 Constellation §13.16.9를 anchor로 읽고; 5 names는 이미 v2.5.27에서 §13.16.9에 있음). 시드 lib 변경 없음.
